Preface.
After I completed this book for you, O Sons, which is the last [book] of medical science with its completion, and I achieved its end through its expositions and explanations, it seemed right to me to complete it for you with this Treatise which is the part about operation, that is, surgery by hand.
Since operation by hand has been laid low in our region, and in our time is entirely absent: until perhaps its science has perished, and its trace has been cut off: and nothing remained of it, except small descriptions in the books of the ancients, which hands have altered: and error and uncertainty befell them, until its purposes were closed off, and its power was diminished: It seemed right to me to revive it with the arrangement of this Treatise according to the way of exposition, and declaration, and abbreviation: and to present the forms of cautery instruments, and other instruments of the work: as it comes from the addition of explanation, and from the hastening of what is necessary.
The reason why a good practitioner of it with his hand is not found in this time of ours, is: because the art of medicine is long, and its author needs to be exercised beforehand in the science of anatomy, which Galen narrated, until he knows the uses of the limbs, and their forms, and their connections, and separation, and has knowledge of bones, and nerves, and muscles, and their number, and their exits, and of the pulsing and quiet veins, and their places of exit.
And because of that Hippocrates said, that the name with the name is much, but with work is little, and especially in the art of the hand.
We indeed have already spoken about that in the introduction of this book.
Since whoever is not knowing what we said about anatomy, cannot avoid falling into error, by which men are killed: as I saw many of those, who are formed of this science, and boast about it without knowledge, and without experience.
Which is, because I saw a foolish physician who cut a scrofulous abscess in a woman's neck, and cut certain arteries in the neck: wherefore the woman's blood flowed, until she fell dead between his hands.
And I saw another physician, who presumed to extract a stone from a man, who had advanced in age, and the stone was large.
He therefore reached it, and extracted it with a piece of the bladder.
Wherefore the man died on the third day.
And I indeed had already been called to extract it: and I saw from the size of the stone, and the condition of the patient, that he would die.
And I saw another physician, who accepted payment from one of the Dukes of our land for medicine: and it happened to a black eunuch, who was with him, that there was a fracture in his leg near the heel: and the physician hastened with his ignorance, and bound the fracture over the wound with cushions, and splints with strong binding, and did not allow the wound to breathe.
Then he released him according to his desires.
Then he left him for several days, and ordered him not to loosen the bandage: and it remained thus until his leg became swollen, and his foot, and came to destruction.
Therefore I was called to him: and I hurried to loosen the bandage: and tranquility followed, and he escaped from his pains.
However, corruption was already confirmed in the limb: and I could not restrain it.
Therefore the corruption did not cease to spread in the limb, until it perished.
And I saw another physician, who pierced a cancerous abscess: and it became ulcerated after days, until its malignancy increased with its owner.
Which is because when cancer is pure from melancholic humor, then one should not approach it with iron at all, unless it is in a limb that can tolerate having all of it cut off.
And because of that, O Sons, it is necessary for you to know that operation by hand is divided into two divisions: namely, operation associated with health: and operation with which there is danger in most conditions.
And I have already warned in every place of this book where an operation occurs in which there is terror and fear.
Therefore it is necessary for you to beware of that and leave it alone: so that fools may not find a way to speak and dishonor.
Therefore take measure with care and protection, and your patients with ease and firmness, and use the better way leading by God's grace to health and praiseworthy success: and leave terrible diseases of difficult healing: and remove your souls from that which makes you fear, lest hesitation enter upon you in your faith and your benefit.
For it is more remaining to your glory, and more sublime in this world, and finally to your measures.
For Galen has already said in some of his admonitions.
Do not treat a bad disease: lest you be named bad physicians.
I have already divided this Treatise according to three Chapters. ¶
Chapter First.
On Cautery with fire, and Cautery with sharp medicine, chaptered, and ordered from head to feet, and forms of instruments, and iron tools of Cautery: and everything that is necessary in operation. ¶
Chapter Second.
On cutting and perforation, bloodletting and cupping, and wounds: and extraction of arrows, and similar to that: and all chaptered, ordered with forms of instruments. ¶
Chapter Third.
On restoration, and dislocation, and treatment of torsion, and similar to that: chaptered, ordered from head to feet, and forms of instruments.
Glory to God Alone.
The Surgical Book of Albucasis.
Part I.
¶ On the Benefit and Harm of Cautery: and which complexions it suits, and at what time: and whether with iron or gold.
Chapter I.
But Before Indeed I recall operation with it, it is necessary that I speak of the quality of its Benefits, and of its Harms: and in which complexion it should be administered.
I say therefore, that discourse on the quality of the benefit of Cautery, and its harm, is a lengthy discourse, and subtle, a science, and a hidden secret.
Indeed many wise men have spoken about it, and disagreed about it: and for me a little of their discourse suffices, fearing prolongation.
I say therefore, that Cautery is universally beneficial for every complexion that is with matter and without matter: except for two complexions, which are the hot complexion without matter, and the dry complexion without matter.
However, regarding the hot and dry complexion with matter, they disagreed.
For some said that Cautery is beneficial in it.
And others said the opposite of this, namely that Cautery is not suitable in illness which is from heat and dryness: since the nature of fire is heat: and it is unsuitable that a hot and dry illness be cured with something hot and dry.
And he who says the opposite of this said: that through Cautery benefit occurs in every hot and dry illness which happens in human bodies: since when you compare the human body, and its humors, to the complexion of fire, you find the human body cold.
And I indeed say through his discourse: because experiment has already revealed this to me several times.
However, none should attempt this unless they have already been tested and trained in the chapter of Cautery with ultimate training, and has known the diversity of human complexions, and the disposition of illnesses in themselves, and their causes, and their symptoms, and their duration.
Concerning the remaining complexions there is no fear upon you: and especially in cold and wet illnesses.
For all physicians have agreed about these: and they have not disagreed about the benefit with Cautery in them.
And know, sons, that from the secret of treatment by Cautery with fire, and its goodness over Cautery with burning medicine is: since fire is simple, whose action does not reach except to the member that is cauterized: and does not harm another member connected with it, except with small harm.
But the action of burning medicine reaches that which is distant from the members: and perhaps causes in the member an illness difficult to heal, and perhaps kills.
Fire however, because of its subtlety and the goodness of its substance, does not do that, unless it is excessive.
This has indeed become known to us through experiment, because of long service and study with the art, and standing upon the truth of things: and because of that I am excused from length of discourse.
And if it were not that it is not permitted in this book of mine, I would bring you a hidden secret about fire, and the quality of its operation in bodies of its expulsion, by which it expels illnesses with philosophical demonstrative discourse, which would be sharpened by your minds.
And know, sons, that they disagree about the time in which it is suitable to perform cautery, and they place the best time as spring.
And I say that cauterization is suitable at any time: because the harm that occurs due to timing is outweighed by the benefit that is drawn from cauterization.
And especially if cauterization is for pains among necessary, severe, urgent pains, which do not tolerate delay: because it is feared from them that harm may occur which is greater than the small harm entering because of timing.
And do not let it fall into your minds, O sons, that which only the common people and foolish physicians believe, namely that the illness which is cured by cauterization never returns: and they make this a rule, but things are not as they think: because cauterization is nothing but a substitute for medicine, which alters the constitution and dries up the humors which are the causes why pains occur.
However, cauterization surpasses medicine through the speed of its effectiveness, and the power of its operation, and the vehemence of its dominion: and it is possible that the illness may return at some time according to the constitution of the sick person, and the location of their illness, and its strength: and what is prepared in their body from the accumulation of superfluities in it: and what reaches it in its acquisition from foods, and similar things from causes, unless it is an illness in which cauterization is administered.
A subtle illness in a member with few superfluities and humors, like cauterization of a tooth for pain, and similar to it, it is indeed possible that that pain may not return in it.
But this happens in few cases.
But again the saying of the common people, that cauterization is the last resort of medicine, is a correct saying: not in the way that they intend it: since they believe that there is no cure that helps with medicine, nor with anything else after the setting of cauterization.
The matter is actually contrary to that, and the intention that cauterization is the last resort of medicine is nothing but that when we administer modes of treatment in any of the illnesses, and those medicines do not help: then we administer cauterization at the end of the matter, and it helps: then from this it follows that cauterization is the last resort of medicine, not according to the intention which the common people and many foolish physicians understand.
The ancients moreover said that cauterization with gold is better than cauterization with iron: and they did not say that except because of the evenness of gold, and the sublimity of its substance: and they said that the site of cauterization does not produce pus.
But this is not absolutely true: since I have already tested it, and found that it does not do that in certain bodies as opposed to others.
And cauterization with it is good, and better than with iron, as they said.
However when you heat the cautery in fire made from gold, it is not clear to you when it is heated according to the amount that you want, because of the redness of gold: and when cold hurries to it, and if you increase the heating upon it, it melts in the fire, and turns into sheets.
Therefore the practitioner falls from it into occupation: and because of that cauterization with iron among us is quicker and closer, from correctness to operation.
And I indeed have already arranged this Chapter on Cauterization, according to chapters: and I arranged them from head to feet: so that they might ease for the seeker that which he wants from it.
¶ On the method of cauterizing the Head at the coronal suture.
Chapter II.
Here cauterization helps against the dominion of humidity and coldness over the brain: which two are causes of headache, and abundance of fluid flow from the head to the parts of eyes and ears, and abundance of sleep, and tooth pain, and throat pain: and universally every illness which occurs from coldness, like paralysis, and headaches, epilepsy, and apoplexy, and similar things from illnesses.
The method of cauterization is that you should instruct the sick person: that they should be evacuated first with purgative medicine cleansing the head for three nights, or four, according to what the strength of the sick person requires, and their age, and their custom.
Then command him to have his head shaved with a razor.
Then have him sit squarely before you, such that he has placed his hands upon his chest.
Then place the base of your palm above the bridge of his nose between his eyes.
Wherever your middle finger reaches, mark that spot with ink.
Then heat the Olive-shaped Cautery: of which this is the form.
Then place it on the spot marked with ink, descending with your hand gradually restrained, and rotate it.
Then lift your hand quickly, and examine the spot.
If you see that a portion of bone the size of an alkiel or a zeuherb has been exposed, then lift your hand.
And if not, repeat with the same iron, or with another if it has cooled: until you see the bones I told you about.
Then take some salt, and dissolve it in water, and soak cotton in it, and place it on the spot: and leave it for three days.
Then place cotton soaked in butter on it, and leave it on the spot until the fire scab is destroyed.
Then treat it with tetrapharmacon ointment until it heals.
They have said that the longer the wound remains open, the more pus it releases: therefore it is better and more beneficial.
And some of them said to cauterize the skin down to the bone: and hold the Cautery until some thickness of bone is burned.
Then scrape away what has been burned from the bone, then treat it.
And others say that one should proceed with the cautery to the ultimate point, until it makes a strong impression in the bone, so that the bone falls away, which becomes like the form of a carat: or the instrument that women use with a small alphabet infusion: and they believe that vapors of the head are expelled from this place, and the wound should be left open for a long time.
Then it should be treated until it consolidates.
However, these two types of Cautery do not seem to me at all except in certain people by way of fear.
And leaving it alone, in my opinion, is better for their safety.
For the head is weakened by the breaking of its natural continuity: as we have witnessed in other limbs: and especially when the patient's head is naturally weak: and indeed the first species of Cautery is safer and better in my opinion, and I use it: therefore operate with it safely.
¶ On the method of cauterizing the head for pain in the whole head.
Chapter III.
When chronic pain occurs in the whole head: and it persists in the patient, and he uses hieras, and cochias, and head purgatives, and oils, and poultices.
And especially if it has already been cauterized with one cautery, which we described, and none of those things helps him: then consider.
For if the patient's head is of strong natural creation, and is not weak, and he experiences severe cold: then cauterize with another cautery slightly below that one.
Then cauterize him over every corner of his head with the cautery, until it passes through the skin, and exposes bone to the quantity we described.
And cauterize him with one cautery at the back of his head, in the place which is called the vessel: and it is the place where the cupping glass is placed: and lift your hand in this, and do not expose the bone.
For the patient experiences because of that severe pain, different from the pain of all other cauteries of the head.
And I will discuss this Cautery in its place: and it is necessary that the cautery, with which the corners of the head and its back are cauterized, be more subtle than the cautery with which the middle of the head is cauterized.
And this is its form.
On the method of cauterizing in migraine, both with burning medicine and with iron.
Chapter 4.
When pain occurs in part of the head and migraine, or the pain extends to the eye, and it is evacuated with medicines that cleanse the head, and the remaining treatment that I mentioned in the division of diseases is administered, and all that does not help: then cauterization in it is according to two methods: either cauterization with sharp burning medicine or with iron.
Cautery with sharp burning medicine is when you take one clove of garlic, and peel it, and cut off its ends from both sides.
Then cut the site of pain at the temple with a broad lancet, until there is a space under the skin in which the clove can be held.
Therefore insert it under the skin until it is hidden: then bind it with a compress with appropriate pressure, and leave it for about fifteen hours then loosen it, and remove the garlic, and leave the wound for two or three days: afterward place cotton soaked in butter on it, until the site produces pus: then treat it with ointment until it heals.
And if you wish, do this with certain burning medicines, which I wrote about in the twelfth treatise, concerning burning Medicines.
But its cauterization with iron is according to this method.
Heat the Cautery, whose form is this.
And it is called Clavilis: because the form of its head is like the form of a nail, in which there is some curvature, and in its middle there is a small protrusion.
Then place it on the site, and hold your hand steady: and rotate the iron gradually with speed: and let the amount that is burned of the thickness of the skin be about half of it.
And lift your hand, so that the artery which is below is not burned, and bleeding occurs.
Then soak cotton in salt water, and place it on the site, and leave it for three days: then place cotton with butter: afterward treat with ointment until it heals.
And if you wish, cauterize this migraine with the second knife-like end of the Cautery.
And beware of cutting the artery in this migraine, especially if not chronic.
On the method of cauterizing in chronic migraine.
Chapter 5.
When you treat migraine with what we mentioned from the preceding treatment, and what we mentioned in the division of diseases, and the treatment does not help: and you see from the disease that what we mentioned from the first cautery with medicine or with cautery with fire is not sufficient, then it is necessary that you heat the knife-like Cautery until it becomes white after you mark the site of pain with a line whose length is half a finger or thereabouts: and lower your hand once, and press it until you cut the artery and reach the bone.
However, it is necessary for you to beware of the continuity of the jawbone, which moves during chewing, lest the side or the nerve that moves it be burned, whereupon spasm occurs.
And be on guard and cautious about the bleeding of the artery which has been cut.
For in cutting it there is danger, especially for one who is ignorant of what he is doing, and is not studious nor experienced: and abandons the operation with it at first.
And I will come with the remembrance of the management of bleeding occurring from the artery according to its method, and in its place in this book.
But if you see from the disease that this Cautery is not sufficient for it, and you see the body of the patient tolerating cautery in the middle of the head, as we narrated, treat the wound until it heals.
And if you wish, administer the Cautery which we mentioned in the chapter on extraction of the artery with the Cautery having two knives.
For it is better cauterization than this and more beneficial.
On the method of cauterization for ear pain.
Chapter 6.
When pain occurs in the ear from cold, and is treated with solvents, and the remaining treatment which we described in the division, and the pain is not removed, then cauterize with fire: and this is what is called the Point, whose form is this.
Then puncture with it after heating it around the entire ear, as it revolves: or around both, if the pain is in both simultaneously.
And distance yourself with the cautery from the root of the ear a little, after you have marked the places with ink: and let the amount of cauterization be ten points in each ear, or thereabouts.
Then treat the areas until they heal.
On the method of cauterization for Facial Paralysis.
Chapter 7.
Facial paralysis which is treated with cauterization is only from the types that occur from phlegm, according to what we said in the division of diseases.
And avoid cauterization of the type that occurs from dryness and spasm of the nerve.
When you treat this type of facial paralysis with hierae [medicines], and head purgatives, and gargles, and your treatment doesn't help, then you should cauterize the patient with three cauteries: one at the root of the ear, and the second a little below from its temple, and the third at the junction of the two lips.
And place your cautery on the opposite side of the affected part.
For the softening occurs only in the part that appears healthy.
And the form of cauterization is that you cauterize with the cautery in line with the upper extremity of the ear slightly below the horn of the head: and another at the temple: whose length should be according to the length of the thumb.
And lower your hand with the cautery until half the thickness of the skin is burned.
And this is the form of the cautery, and it is a type of knife-like instrument, whose form was mentioned before: however it is not much more subtle than it, as you see: and the knife in it should be slightly more thick than usual.
Then treat the areas with what was previously mentioned: until it heals.
On the method of cauterization in chronic Apoplexy.
Chapter 8.
When apoplexy becomes chronic, and you treat it with what we mentioned, and your medication doesn't help, and the patient doesn't have fever, then cauterize him with four cauteries above every horn of his head, and a cautery in the middle of the head, as we said, and a cautery in the back of the head, according to what preceded: and let the method of cautery be according to what preceded.
Also cauterize with a cautery above the mouth of the stomach: and this is most ultimate.
Then let it be treated with what preceded.
On the method of cauterization for Memory Loss.
Chapter 9.
First, the patient should be given great hierae to drink, and pills that purify the brain.
Then shave the patient's entire head, and place on his occiput the mustard plaster described in the treatise on plasters: and apply it several times.
For this is a method of cautery: and do it according to the same order that I described there.
If therefore he is healed by that, it is good.
If not: then make three cauteries in the posterior part of his head, which should descend from the upper part of the head to the lower part of the eye: and place between each cautery the thickness of a finger.
Then treat the cautery with what preceded.
But if you want an addition, and the patient can tolerate it: then make him a cautery in the middle.
And if you want an addition: then cauterize him above the two horns.
Then treat him until he heals: and let the cautery be olive-shaped according to the form which was mentioned before.
On the method of cauterization in Paralysis and softening.
Chapter 10.
You should proceed in purifying the head with hierae, and with what we mentioned.
Then shave the patient's head: afterward cauterize him with a cautery in the middle of the head, and a cautery above every horn of the head, and a cautery above its posterior part, and three above the vertebrae of the neck.
But if you need more than those in the disease of softening of the body, and the patient can tolerate it, and the disease is severe: then cauterize him with four cauteries above the vertebrae of the back, and finish with the cautery, until most of the skin is burned, and lift your hand.
Then treat him until he heals: and thus the olive-shaped cautery.
On the method of cauterizing in Epilepsy.
Chapter 11.
An epileptic person should not be cauterized, except one whose epilepsy is from phlegm.
Therefore it is necessary that you first cleanse their brain with hierae [herbal medicines], and with the remaining treatment which we mentioned in the division: when the patient is grown, or is tolerant in accepting medicines.
If however it is a child, who does not tolerate medicines, then administer gargling, and chewing substances that cleanse the brain, before that for many days with improvement of foods.
Then shave their head, afterwards cauterize it with one cautery in the middle of the head, according to what was previously described in the method: and with another cautery at the back of the head, and over every corner of their head with a cautery.
But if the patient is strong, and is tolerant, then cauterize them with the cauteries which I described for one having paralysis and softening of the body over the vertebrae of the neck and vertebrae of the back: and let the cautery be olive-shaped according to the method which preceded.
If however the patient is a child, then apply a fine cautery, according to this method.
On the method of cauterizing in Melancholia.
Chapter 12.
When the causes of melancholia are corrupt humidities and thick phlegm, then cauterize them with the cauteries which we described for one having paralysis.
And if the cause of melancholia is an excess inclining to melancholy, and the patient's body is moist, then give them to drink what will cleanse their brain, according to what preceded in the division: then shave the patient's head, and afterwards make a properly made circular pad from linen, like a circle.
Then place it in the middle of the head: and let the patient sitting square be held from all sides.
Then present the liniment.
And it is most worthy from old sheep's butter.
And heat it over fire with moderate heating to a measure which a finger tolerates when it is inserted into it.
Then empty it in the middle of their head in a circle, and leave it until it cools.
Do that to the patient once every week, with the rest of their good regimen, until they are healed.
Or if you wish, cauterize them making many small points, beyond which you do not hold the hand with the cautery: rather let it be by sensing.
For this type of cautery moistens the brain with its quality.
Then place cotton soaked in butter or chicken fat over it.
On the method of cauterizing in water descending to the eye [cataract].
Chapter 13.
When the beginning of water in the eye becomes clear to you through the signs which I mentioned in the division, then begin and give the patient to drink what will cleanse their head.
And guard them from all moistures, and make them sit in the bath, fasting for some days.
Then command them to shave their head, and cauterize them in the middle of their head.
Then cauterize them over the two temples with two cauteries, if it is the beginning of water descending in both eyes together: or from one side, if it is the beginning of water in one eye: and cut with the cautery all veins and arteries which are under the skin: and let the cauteries in it be long in the width of the temples: and beware of blood flow.
But if you see any of it, then cut it off immediately with whatever medicine is possible: and I will come with wisdom, which is in the extraction of arteries, and cutting them, and caution against blood flow.
And sometimes it is cauterized in the neck, under the two bones, with two cauteries ultimately produced.
On the method of cauterizing in Ancient Tears.
Chapter 14.
When the tears of the eyes are ancient, constant: and are over veins and arteries which are manifest externally on the head, it is verified that this is from cold, phlegmatic superfluities: then cauterize with the same cautery that I narrated in the beginning of descending water, with a cautery in the middle of the head, and two cauteries over the two temples, and two cauteries in the neck under the two bones.
And if you need addition, then cauterize them on every side of the eye cavity, over the extremity of the eyebrow with a small cautery.
On the method of cauterizing for foul smell of the Nose.
Chapter 15.
When you treat it with what we described in the division, and the treatment doesn't help: then hurry, and give the patient to drink for three nights: then shave his head, and cauterize it with a medium cautery, using an olive-shaped cautery.
Then cauterize it with a nail-shaped cautery using two cauteries, above the two eyebrows slightly under the hair.
And be careful of the artery, lest you cut it.
And this is the form of the nail-shaped cautery.
On the method of cauterizing for laxity of the Eyelid.
Chapter 16.
When the eyelid of the eye becomes lax from illness or moisture: then cauterize the eyelid with one cautery, using this crescent-shaped cautery.
And if you wish, cauterize it above the two eyebrows slightly with two cauteries on each side: and let them be distant from the two temples: and let the length of each cautery be according to the length of the eyebrow: and do not extend your hand with the cautery, but rather according to the amount that burns a third of the eyelid.
And this is the form of the cautery according to this method of the crescent-shaped cautery.
On the method of cauterizing the Eyelid when hairs turn inward pricking the eye.
Chapter 17.
Cauterization in this case is according to two methods: either cautery with fire: or cautery with burning medicine.
In cautery with fire, instruct the patient beforehand to let his hairs grow, if he is among those who trim them, until they become long and even.
If however they prick him at their growth: then bind his eyes with a band, so they don't move, until they grow.
When therefore they grow and become even, then place the patient's head in your lap: then mark on his eyelid with ink, a mark that should be in the shape of a myrtle leaf: and let the beginning of the mark be near the hairs.
Then place cotton soaked in egg white: or in psyllium mucilage over the eye.
Then heat the cautery, whose form is this.
Then cauterize over the figure which you marked gradually in many passes, until the surface of the skin is burned, which is like the figure of a myrtle leaf, all visible specifically.
And the sign of the success of your work is: that if you see the eyelid of the eye has contracted, and the hairs raised at the point where they prick the eye.
Therefore lift your hand then: and leave it for three days.
Then place Cotton with butter on it, until the scab falls off.
Then treat it with ointment until it heals.
But if any of the hairs return after a while, and the eyelid becomes lax: then repeat the Cautery over that place, as you did at first.
If however the hairs are in the lower [eyelid]: then cauterize it, until it rises to its natural place: and becomes even so that the hairs don't prick the eye.
On the method of cauterizing with burning medicine in the same case.
Chapter 18.
It is that you should instruct the patient to let the hairs grow until they become long and even.
Make from paper or cloth the shape of a myrtle leaf.
Then take of known soap and of unslaked lime, of each one ounce or thereabouts: then grind them together with good grinding, and do this quickly, so that it does not cool.
Then spread this over the paper which you made in the shape of a myrtle leaf, and place it over the eyelid of one eye, or both.
And place under the eye cotton soaked in egg white: and let the patient's head be in your lap.
And place your index finger over the medicine, and press it slightly.
And move it whenever the patient feels the stinging of the medicine: for its stinging feels like fire.
While therefore the stinging that he feels persists, then leave the medicine, and move it with your finger.
When therefore the stinging subsides, then remove the medicine, and wash the eye with water.
And observe then, if you see the eyelid rising, as it rises during contraction with fire, or with incision, it is good: and if not, then repeat with the medicine over the same place, where the medicine did not make an impression, and did not blacken, until your operation is even, and the eye contracts.
Then place upon it cotton with butter, until the burnt skin is removed.
Then treat it with diaphinicon ointment, or another, until it heals.
And it is necessary for you during the operation to guard with utmost care, lest anything from the medicine falls into the eye.
But if the eyelid softens after days, and some of the hairs fight in the eye, then repeat the medicine over that place which is softened from the eyelid specifically, as you did at first.
Then treat it until it heals.
And this is the shape of the myrtle leaf.
And know that people's eyes differ in size, both large and small.
Therefore according to that should be your consideration: and the path of correctness is not hidden from one who has studied this art.
On the method of cauterizing in lachrymal fistula.
Chapter 19.
When you treat a fistula with what we have described in the divisions of diseases, and your treatment does not help: then, it is necessary that you cauterize it according to this method.
Command the patient to place his head in your lap, and let an assistant hold his head between his hands in such a way that he does not move, nor shake with his head.
Then place cotton soaked in egg white, or in psyllium mucilage over his eye: then heat the cautery, whose shape is this.
Let it be hollow, like the shape of a vulture's feather quill at one end, with which the cauterization is done: and if you wish it may penetrate to the other end, and if you wish it may be held up thus.
However, this hollow one is better for your work.
Then squeeze the fistula, if it is open, and extract the pus from it, and dry it: and if it is not open, then open it, and extract its pus.
Then place upon it the cautery, which should be very hot.
And hold your hand with it a little while during cauterization away from the eye, toward the nose, so that your hand does not err, or the patient become disturbed: and you place the cautery in the fat of the eye, and corrupt it.
If therefore you reach in the beginning of your cauterization all the way to the bone, it will be good.
And if not: then repeat the cauterization once, or twice, if you need that: and leave it for three days.
Then place cotton with butter, and treat it with drying ointment, until it heals.
But if forty days pass, and it does not heal: then place upon it sharp corrosive medicine, until the bone is exposed: and scrape it according to what comes in its chapter.
And there is another method of cauterizing a fistula, which some of the ancients have described.
Look to the location of the fistula, and split it open: then place in this split a thin camahan, that is, a thin tube, whose form is this.
And pour into it the quantity of a drachm of melted lead, and hold your hand with the tube with a good grip, and the patient should not move at all, so that the melted lead does not run or reach their eye.
And it is necessary that you place over the patient's eye cotton soaked in egg white, or in water.
For the lead burns the site of the fistula, and heals it with wonderful healing.
If the fistula is healed with what we have described of cautery and treatment, it is good.
And if not, then it is necessary to work on the opening of the nose, and redirect the fistula to the passage of the nose, according to what will come in its own proper place.
¶ On the method of cauterizing in fissures of the Lips.
Chapter 20.
Often fissures occur in the lip, which are called Pili, and especially in the lips of children.
When therefore you treat these fissures with what we have described in the division of diseases, and the treatment is not effective, then heat a small knife-like cautery, according to this form.
And let its concavity be according to the thinness of the knife.
Then place it heated quickly in these fissures, until the cautery reaches the depth of the fissures.
Then treat it with wax salve until it heals.
¶ On the method of cauterizing in fistula of the Mouth.
Chapter 21.
When an abscess occurs in the root of the gum, or in the palate, or in the roots of teeth: then it makes pus, and bursts: afterwards it becomes chronic, and pus runs, and becomes a fistula: then you treat it, and if treatment is not effective, then it is necessary that you heat a cautery according to the size that will fit in the fistula.
Then introduce it heated into the opening of the fistula, and hold your hand, until the heated iron reaches its depth and its end: do this once, or twice.
Then treat it after that with what we have described of treatment until it is cured.
If therefore the discharge is cut off, and it heals, it will be good.
And if not, then it is necessary to expose the area, and remove the corrupted bone according to what will come in its chapter.
¶ On the method of cauterizing in Gums and loosened Teeth.
Chapter 22.
When the gum is softened because of moisture, and the teeth move, and you treat it with medicines, and it is not effective: then place the head of the patient in your lap.
Then heat a cautery, whose form will come after this, so that you place the tube over the tooth: and introduce into it the heated cautery quickly: and hold your hand a little while, until the patient feels the heat of the fire has reached the root of the tooth.
And lift your hand: then repeat the cautery several times, according to what you wish.
Then let the patient fill their mouth with salt water, and hold it for one hour: and spit it out.
For the loose tooth becomes firm, and the softened gum tightens, and the corrupt moisture dries up.
On the method of cauterizing for tooth pain.
Chapter 23.
When tooth pain is due to cold, or there is cold in it, or a worm, and treatment with medicines does not help: then Cautery for it is according to two methods: either Cautery with butter or cautery with fire.
The cautery with butter is when you take cow's butter and boil it in an iron spoon or in a vessel.
Then take cotton and wrap it around the end of a probe.
Then submerge it in the boiled butter and place it quickly on the painful tooth, and hold it until it cools: then repeat this several times, until the power of the heat reaches the root of the tooth.
And if you wish, submerge wool or cotton in cold butter, and place it on the aching tooth: and place a heated iron over it, until the heat reaches the depth of the tooth's cavity.
The cauterization with fire is when you use a bronze tube or an iron tube.
And there should be some thickness in its body, so that the sharpness of the fire does not reach the patient's mouth.
Then heat the Cautery, whose form will come: and place it on that tooth: and hold your hand until the Cautery cools.
Do this several times, for the pain will be removed either on that same day or another day.
And in the application of that Cautery, the patient should fill their mouth with good butter and hold it for one hour: then spit it out.
And this is the form of the Cautery.
Cauterize with whichever end you wish according to what is possible: and this is the form of the Tube.
On the method of cauterizing Scrofula.
Chapter 24.
When Scrofula is from phlegm and from cold humors, and they are not responsive to digestion through medicines, and you want their digestion quickly: then heat a hollow Cautery, whose form is this.
Having two open ends, so that smoke may exit during Cautery from the other end: and place it heated on the abscess once, and a second time if you need it, until it reaches the depth of the abscess.
If the abscess is small: then apply the Cautery according to the size of the abscess.
Then leave it for three days, and place cotton soaked in butter on it, until what the fire burned is removed.
Then treat it with tooth ointment until the form of the tube heals.
On the method of cauterizing for hoarseness of voice and constriction of breathing.
Chapter 25.
When humors overcome the pulmonary canal, and especially when this is with coldness of complexion, then it is necessary that the patient first be evacuated with purgative medicines.
Then cauterize them in the depression at the root of the throat: and be careful not to reach the throat with the Cautery, nor in the skin, except a little of it.
Then cauterize them with another cautery at the joint of the neck at its last vertebra finally: and let the Cautery be nail-shaped according to the method that preceded.
Then treat them with what preceded until they heal.
On the method of cauterizing in diseases of the Lungs and Cough.
Chapter 26.
When Cough and disease of the Lungs are from cold humors, and the patient does not have fever, nor consumption, and the disease is chronic: then cauterize them with two cauteries above the collarbone in depressed, smooth, empty places.
And with another cautery in the middle of the chest between the two breasts: and let the cautery be tube-shaped according to the form that preceded.
And if you wish, let your cauterization be by puncturing with the cautery which is called Point, whose form preceded in the puncturing for ear pain: and let the points be from thirty points up to about others.
Then treat them with what preceded until they heal.
And now let there be a cautery having three branches: according to this form.
Whereby cauterization is made easier, when you make with it three Cauteries at once.
On the method of cauterizing in the Armpit, in dislocation of the Humerus.
Chapter 27.
When the head of the humerus is dislocated due to humidity, and is not fixed at the time of its return from its dislocation, until this becomes a habit of returning, then it dislocates from a small motion that occurs as we have already testified, then it is necessary that you first reduce the dislocation.
Then let the patient lie on his back, or on his healthy side.
Then lift the skin, which is in the inner Armpit upwards with the fingers of your left hand: and if the joint dislocates inward.
Then heat a Cautery having two prongs.
Whose form is this.
Then cauterize the skin, until it penetrates it to the other side, and the figure of cauterization will come with four cauteries.
And sometimes cauterization is done with a cautery having three prongs, whereby the figure of cauterization then becomes six cauteries: and the prongs are according to the thinness of the probe.
And this is the form of the cautery having three prongs.
And sometimes one is added above this method, whereby there are eight cauteries.
Then place crushed leeks with salt over the cautery.
Then have the patient remain still, so that the limb does not move for some time, until it strengthens.
And if the dislocation is upward, and this rarely happens, then cauterize it above the shoulder with a nail-shaped cautery, or with many cauteries by puncturing.
For the joint becomes firm, and humidity is removed: and the patient is healed.
On the method of cauterizing the Stomach.
Chapter 28.
When cold and many humidities occur in the Stomach, until they draw it from its complexion, and catarrhs multiply to it, and you have tried continuous modes of treatment, and it does not help: then it is necessary that the patient lie on his back, and extend his legs and his hands.
Then cauterize with three cauteries, a cautery below the breast bone the measure of one finger with a nail-shaped cautery, and two cauteries below from the two sides of one cautery, until the figure of the cauteries becomes triangular.
And separate between both so they do not join when they make pus.
And let the depth of the cautery be the measure of two-thirds of the thickness of the skin.
And let the figure of the cauteries be according to this form without addition: and if you wish cauterize with a large cautery in the middle of the stomach according to this form: and let the cautery by which this is done be one according to the figure of a circle according to this form.
And the stomach is cauterized by puncturing for one who is terrified of this cautery: and it is, that you mark upon the stomach points according to the quantity that you wish with ink: then cauterize it with a point cautery: then treat it with the treatment which preceded until it heals.
On the method of cauterizing a cold Liver.
Chapter 29.
When pain occurs in the Liver from coldness and humidity, or from thick windiness, until it departs from its natural complexion in excessive departure, and the patient is treated with what we have said, and it does not benefit in that: then it is necessary that the patient lie on his neck, and you mark with ink three cauteries according to this figure, and this same quantity over the Liver below the hypochondria, where the elbow of the person reaches: and let the space that is between every cautery be according to the thickness of a finger: and let the cautery be straight according to the length of the body: and do not press your hand with the cautery much.
And let the quantity of what is burned from the thickness of the skin be the quantity of half of it not added: and let the patient be standing on his feet.
If however he is not standing, then let him be lying, who has already extended his legs and raised his arms.
This is the form of the cautery.
And it is indeed possible for you to cauterize these cauteries with a knife-shaped cautery, when you have subtlety and prudence in the art.
And guard yourself, that you do not proceed ultimately in cauterization, and the thickness of the whole skin is burned, whereby the whole body is burned, and it reaches to the intestines: since the skin there is thin, know therefore that.
¶ On the method of cauterizing liver abscesses.
Chapter 30.
When an abscess occurs, and you want to know if that swelling is in the liver tissue or in its membrane: then if it is in the liver tissue, the patient is seized by pain and heaviness without sharpness; and if it is in the liver membrane, there is severe sharpness with the pain; and you see that its treatment has already exhausted the physicians.
Therefore, the patient should lie back on their neck.
Then mark the location of the abscess with ink; then heat the cautery that resembles a rod.
And this is its form.
And cauterize with it one cautery until the whole skin is burned and reaches the peritoneum, until all the pus comes out; then treat it with the treatment for abscesses until it heals.
And one should not use this type of cautery unless one's study in the medical art has been prolonged, and through whose hands these illnesses have occurred with some experimentation; only then should one dare to perform such an operation.
But to leave it alone is, in my opinion, better.
¶ On the method of cauterizing in Pleurisy.
Chapter 31.
The ancients spoke of cautery with birthwort roots for cold pleurisy in this way.
That is, take from the dried long birthwort roots one of the longer roots that can be found, and let it be about the thickness of a finger.
Then submerge it in oil and light it in the fire.
Then cauterize with one cautery in the area between the joint of the collarbone with the neck, and with two small cauteries below the guidezi slightly inclined to the part below the beard.
And also with two cauteries in the area between the fifth and sixth rib inclined slightly backward; and another cautery in the middle of the chest, and another above the stomach.
And three cauteries from behind: one between the shoulder blades, and two cauteries on the two sides of the chest, below the cautery that is between the shoulder blades.
And you should not press your hand with the cautery, but rather it should be evident on the skin by smell.
And some ancients have said that there are among men those who use an iron cautery similar to a rod: and they heat it and insert it between the ribs until it reaches the abscess itself and the pus comes out, as we said regarding the liver abscess.
But in this perforation with cautery there is the fear that either the patient dies immediately, or a fistula occurs in the place, for which there is no cure.
¶ On the method of cauterizing the Spleen Chapter 32.
When you treat a disease of the spleen with what we mentioned about treatment in the division of diseases, and your treatment does not help, then cautery for it is according to three methods, all of which are correct.
One of which is that you make three or four cauteries in a line according to the length of the spleen following the pattern of liver cauteries, whose form preceded.
And let there be between each cautery the width of a finger, or a little more.
And let the method of cautery be what we mentioned in the liver cautery equally.
And do not press your hand with the cautery: and let the patient lie on their back.
And another method of cauterization is: that you heat a cautery having two prongs, which we mentioned in the chapter on shoulder dislocation: and lift the skin that is in line with the spleen, where the patient's left elbow reaches: and let your lifting of the skin be according to the width of the body, so that the cauteries fall according to the length of the body.
Then insert the two prongs very hot, until you penetrate the skin with them from the other side: then remove the cautery: thus four cauteries are made.
And if you wish, cauterize with another cautery having three prongs.
Then treat the cautery after you let it discharge pus for many days: for it is more beneficial than the other treatments that preceded.
On the Method of Cauterizing in Dropsy.
Chapter 33.
Cauterization is not applicable in dropsy, except specifically in ascites.
When you treat a dropsical patient with the methods of treatment that we mentioned in the classification, and the treatment is not effective, then you should cauterize them with four cauterizations around the navel, and one cauterization over the stomach, and another cauterization over the liver, and a cauterization over the spleen, and two cauterizations behind the back between the vertebrae, and one directly on the chest, and another directly on the stomach: and let the depth of cauterization be close to the thickness of the skin.
Then leave the cautery open, so that it may discharge pus for a long time.
And do not cease treating the patient after cauterization with this: for it is necessary that two intentions be combined for him: and healing will hasten to him with God's help.
The form of the cautery with which the belly is cauterized should be nail-shaped: according to its previous form: and that with which the back is cauterized should be olive-shaped according to its previous form.
On the Method of Cauterizing Feet and Legs.
Chapter 34.
When they swell in a dropsical patient, and are filled with yellow water: you should cauterize over the top of the Foot in the nocrati, which is between the little finger and the ring finger: and lift your hand with the cautery, and do not twist it: then lift your hand: and do not repeat it at all.
For the yellow water will seep out, and let the cautery be according to this form.
Then make two cauterizations on the two legs on each leg, and let the cautery be made with the knife-edge of the cautery: and let the cautery be made along the length of the leg, one below the knee, and the other lower than it, around the middle of the leg: and two cauteries on each hip: and leave the cautery open without treatment for a long time: so that some of the water may seep out: then treat it with the remaining things we mentioned.
On the Method of Cauterizing in Looseness of the Bowels.
Chapter 35.
When there is looseness of the bowels from cold and moistures, until it weakens the retentive and digestive powers, which are in the stomach and intestines: and this is treated with methods of treatment, and is not cured: and you see the patient able to tolerate cauterization of abundant strength, then cauterize them with a large cautery over their stomach, according to what preceded in cauterization of the stomach with a circular cautery, and four small cauterizations around the navel, with a small nail-shaped cautery: and a cautery over the lower back above the sacrum large, or with two cauteries.
And if you see abundant moistures, and the patient tolerating it, then cauterize them with a cautery over the pubic region, and a cautery over each flank: and perhaps you may add two small cauteries over the stomach near the large one.
For it is a beneficial treatment, whose help does not fail.
On the Method of Cauterizing Hemorrhoids.
Chapter 36.
When in the anus there are many old hemorrhoids, or one, and they are from thick, cold humors, or corrupt moistures, and they are treated with what we mentioned in the classification, and the treatment is not effective: then cauterize with three cauteries over the lower vertebra of the back below the coccyx a little in a triangular pattern, and with a cautery below the navel about two fingers' width.
And if you think that their stomach has become cold, and their food is not being digested, and you see their face swelling, then cauterize them over the stomach with a large cautery, according to what preceded: and with a cautery over their Liver, and another over their Spleen, with a nail-shaped cautery: and leave the cautery open for some time: then treat them until they are healed.
On the method of cauterizing althelul (hemorrhoids) after cutting them off.
Chapter 37.
When you cut off the althelul, then heat a cautery that resembles a rod.
Then insert this heated instrument into the cut althelul: and move your hand until the cautery reaches the opening of the vein from which blood flows: do this once or twice.
If therefore there are many althelul, then cauterize each one with the cautery as we have described.
Then treat them with whatever ointments benefit them until they heal.
And if you cauterize it with a large cautery over the hip, it is most effective in helping.
On the method of cauterizing a fistula in the anus.
Chapter 38.
When the patient does not submit to the incision and procedure which we described in its place, and is frightened of it, perhaps he can be healed with cautery.
When therefore someone develops a fistula, and it becomes chronic, pus flows from it, and corrupted fluids.
Therefore what is most proper is to probe it with a fine probe.
Then determine the depth of it with the probe.
Then heat a cautery which is similar to a rod.
Then insert the heated instrument into the fistula to the same depth that the probe entered.
And repeat the cautery on it until all those corrupted tissues are burned, once, or twice, or three times, according to your need.
And guard yourself from burning a nerve, if there is one there, or a large vein: or if the fistula goes to the body of the bladder, or to the body of the intestine, then guard yourself from all these places.
And do not do this unless the fistula is in a fleshy place: and you think that it is not penetrating.
Then treat the area until it heals.
If however the area seals up, and the discharges cease from it, and it remains so for a long time: then know that it has healed completely.
And if the discharges do not cease from it, then know that it is penetrating, or in its depth there is corrupted bone, or something like that among those things: mention of which will come in its place.
On the method of cauterizing the Kidneys.
Chapter 39.
When pain occurs in the Kidneys from cold, or from thick wind, and because of this the patient's strength diminishes, then you should cauterize him over the back over the kidneys themselves, with a cautery over each kidney with a nail-shaped cautery, mention of which came before.
And perhaps we cauterize him a second time in the same place.
Wherefore three lines will come.
Therefore they will be most effective in helping.
On the method of cauterizing the Bladder.
Chapter 40.
When weakness occurs in the Bladder, and softening from cold and moistures, until the patient cannot retain urine, then cauterize him in the lower part of the abdomen over the Bladder, where the pubic hair begins, and with a cautery on the right side of the abdomen, and another on the left of it: and let the length of that lateral cauterization be according to the size of the thumb joint: and cauterize him with a cautery on the lower back, or with two cauteries, if you need that: and let it be according to what preceded with the nail-shaped cautery.
On the method of cauterizing the Womb.
Chapter 41.
When cold and moistures occur in the Womb, and because of this she is prevented from becoming pregnant, and her menses are corrupted, and their onset is delayed, and pain occurs to her at their arrival, then it is proper that she be cauterized with three cauteries around the navel, as we said in the cauterization of the bladder, and with a cautery over the hip lower on the back, or with two cauteries: and let it be a nail-shaped cautery.
On the method of cauterizing the Hip in dislocation.
Chapter 42.
When mucous humors flow into the hip socket, and become the cause of its exit from its place: and the sign of this is that one leg becomes longer than the other when they are compared: and the site of dislocation is found empty in it.
Therefore you should cauterize the patient on the hip socket itself with a circular cautery: after you mark with ink around the socket, as it revolves: and so that the socket itself falls in the middle of the circle.
And let the cautery be of the form that was previously described in the cauterization of the stomach.
If this cautery is not available to you, then cauterize it with three cauteries, using a large olive-shaped cautery: and let the depth of the cauterization be according to the thickness of the entire skin.
Then treat it until it heals.
On the method of cauterizing in Sciatica.
Chapter 43.
When pain occurs in the hip socket, and cold and humors are the cause of it: and the patient is treated with what we described in the division, and the treatment does not help, and it becomes chronic: then you should free the patient from thick humors with foul pills, or with artificial pills, and similar ones.
Then cauterize him.
And the method of cautery in it is according to two modes: either cautery with burning medicines, or cautery with fire.
Cautery with fire is according to many modes.
One of which is that you cauterize above their hip socket with three triangular cauteries, according to this form.
And make them of good depth, or bad.
And let the space between each cautery be the width of a finger: and let the cautery be olive-shaped.
Sometimes the cautery is made in the middle over the head of the hip itself.
Therefore there are four cauteries.
And if you wish, cauterize with a circle, whose form was previously described in the cauterization of hip dislocation, one: so that the circle contains the entire hip.
And burn through the thickness of the entire skin.
This is the method of cautery in Sciatica, when the pain is adhering to the hip itself, and does not extend to the thigh and leg.
But if it extends to the thigh and leg, then cauterize it with two cauteries above the thigh, above the place where the patient indicates there, where the pain is, and with your cautery above the ankle four fingers toward the outer part slightly: and let the cautery be knife-shaped.
And let the depth of the cautery be according to the depth of the skin's thickness.
But if the patient indicates that the pain extends nearly to the toes of the foot, then cauterize there where he indicates with a point cautery, three, or four, or more, if that is needed.
And if he indicates the pain is below the knee toward the leg, then cauterize there with one knife-shaped cautery.
And in all your cauterization, beware that you do not go so far with the cautery as to burn a nerve, or a major artery, and thereby bring upon the patient severe harm, or contraction.
And I indeed have seen one and another, of those who cauterized above the ankle, and went too far in cauterization, and the leg swelled up, until the swelling reached the foot, and it was all perforated, and the whole foot was corrupted: then diarrhea occurred, and death after that.
If the pain is in both parts simultaneously, cauterize both according to this method.
And certain wise men spoke about cauterization of the hip, whose cautery is of this mode.
Make an iron similar to a forceps, whose diameter should be half a palm: and at its opening it should be according to the thickness of a date pit, or a little less: and within that forceps should be a third forceps.
And let the space between each forceps be the size of a thumb joint: and let the forceps be open on both sides: and let their height be about one joint, or two joints: and make them an iron handle properly fitted to the forceps.
And this is its form.
Then let it be heated in fire until it becomes red and throws off sparks: then let it be placed over the hip socket with the patient lying on their healthy side.
So cauterize it with three round cauteries at once.
Then leave it for three days.
Afterwards dress it with butter: and leave the wound open for many days.
Then treat it with ointment until it heals.
Albucasis said, "O my sons, we have used this type of cautery little, because of its terrifying appearance: and because we find few who can endure it.
However, it is among the good cauteries for one who can bear it, and finds relief with it.
The cautery with burning medicines is done thus: you make two curved pieces having a perforated ring, into which descends the hinge of its gate made of bronze or iron, the length of the wall: in their height there should be two knots, or something like them.
And let the space between both be the width of a finger, and let them be open below and above: and let them hold together, according to this form.
Then place it over the hip socket, with the patient lying on the healthy side.
And press your hand firmly over the hip socket.
Then pour between the two circles hot water, which has been heated somewhat with fire, and hold it for about an hour: and let the patient endure its biting and burning, for he will feel a biting like fire, until the biting subsides.
Then lift your hand with the instrument, and clean off the hot water from the entire hip with fresh water: then leave it for three days.
And put butter on it until the blackness of the burn is removed: and leave it for several days, and pus will flow from it.
For this is ultimate in benefit.
Then treat it with ointments until it heals.
If the pain extends to the thigh or leg: make for it a vessel containing water, just as you did for the hip in the same way.
And this is the method of hot water: and I have already written about it in the treatise on the preparation of medicines.
Take alkali and unslaked lime, one part each: grind both and put them in a new pot whose bottom part is perforated with one small hole, according to the size that a rod might enter it: and place under the bottom of the pot another glazed pot: and pour over the alkali and lime sweet water that covers both by a finger's width: after you compress them well with your hand: and leave the pot until the sharp water descends to the lower part of the glazed pot.
Then collect all that water and pour it over other lime: and strain until it is renewed.
For it will then be of very strong sharpness, which is used in many medical operations and in cauterization of other limbs.
Because it produces the effect of fire itself.
And among the medicines with which the hip is cauterized are also like euphorbias, and cashew honey, and lime with soap, such that both are mixed. ¶
And Galen indeed reported in narration a certain ancient man's cure, by which hip pain and sciatic vein were treated: and he greatly praised its effectiveness.
And he said that he needed no other treatment, and that he was cured in one session, until he reported that he perhaps entered the bath carried and left it already healthy.
And it is thus: take green seitaragi: and if green is not found, take dry, fresh: and grind it well with some fat, and place it on the hip where there is pain, or leg, or in the thigh: and bind it, and leave it for about three hours, or for the time until the patient feels relief from the burning.
Then bring him into the bath.
When therefore his body becomes dewy, put him in the tub.
For the pain recedes, and he is healed.
And know that no one should use cautery with these medicines except after evacuation of the body.
And Dioscorides indeed said that when goat dung is used to cauterize the sciatic vein, it helps it: and the cauterization is done in this way.
Take wool, and soak it in old oil, and place it over the deep spot which is between the toe of the foot and the shin bone, and is closer to the shin bone.
Then take dried goat dung, and inflame it in fire until it becomes charcoal.
Then place it on the wool, and leave it until it is extinguished.
Then repeat that.
Do not cease doing this until the sensation reaches through the middle up to the hip, and the pain subsides.
And this method of cautery is called the Bovine cautery.
¶ On the cauterization of Back pain.
Chapter 44.
Sometimes pain occurs in the Back from many causes, either from a fall, or from a blow, or from excessive evacuation, and similar things, from the infusion of cold and wet material: and cautery indeed is only applicable in this single type, which occurs from the infusion of cold material.
Therefore after evacuating the patient with foul pills and similar things, it is necessary that three lines be made over the Back where the pain is, according to the width of its medial part, after you mark with ink in every line five cauteries, or more according to the amount that comes from the patient's tolerance of his strength: and let the cauterization be done with a pointed cautery.
And if you wish, cauterize with three or four cauteries, with a medium nail-shaped cautery, according to this form.
¶ On the method of cauterizing at the beginning of Hunchback.
Chapter 45.
This illness often occurs in small children.
And the sign of its beginning in children is: that constriction occurs in their breathing during elevation and movement: and you find in the last vertebrae of the Back and its nodes, that it has already begun to protrude above the other vertebrae.
Therefore when you see that, and you wish to do it, then cauterize it with a cautery that is circular according to this form.
And let the cautery take hold equally over every part of the vertebra: and if you wish cauterize around the vertebra with a point cautery in two or three lines: and let the points be close to each other.
Then treat the area until it heals with what we have mentioned.
And beware, do not apply cautery in hunchback which occurs in nerve spasm.
¶ On the method of cauterizing in Gout and pains of the joints.
Chapter 46.
When joint pains are from cold humidities, which are poured out to any members of the body, then when pains occur in the feet, it is the custom of physicians to name that specifically Gout.
Therefore when Gout of cold cause is treated with methods of treatment, and the pains are not removed, then cautery removes them.
And it is that you cauterize it after evacuation around the joint of the feet, with many cauteries: and let the cautery be Olive-shaped.
This is its form.
And if you need to make points on the surface of the foot, then do it with a point cautery.
But if the pains ascend up to the knees, or other joints, and this often occurs, then cauterize above every knee with three or four cauteries on every side, with this same nail-shaped cautery.
If however more than this cautery are necessary for you, then cauterize it.
And do not submerge your hand with the cautery, rather let it be about the thickness of the skin only.
If however the pains ascend to the knees and back: then administer what we said about cautery in its chapter.
But if the pains are in the hands only, then make points around the arm bones, as two lines revolve.
If however pain remains in the fingers, then make points over every joint a point, and over the back of the hand.
If however the pains ascend after days to the elbows or to the shoulders, then cauterize both on every side.
And do not empty the patient from good regimen, from the receiving of medicines.
For if good regimen is maintained, and phlegm is evacuated, he will be healed with God's help with this cautery.
Concerning the method of cauterizing in Ruptures.
Chapter 47.
When a Rupture occurs in the groin, and intestine or omentum descends to the testicle, and it is in its beginning stages and nearby: then it is necessary that you instruct the patient to stop eating on that day.
And he should use laxatives, by which stool may descend from his belly.
Then he should sit before you on his back: and instruct him to hold his breath, until the omentum or intestine comes out or appears.
Then return it with your fingers, and mark with ink below the Rupture above the pubic bone, with a mark whose end is similar to half a circle toward the upper body.
Then heat the cautery, which is of this form, until it becomes white and throws off sparks.
Then return the intestine or omentum to its cavity.
Then let the assistant place his hand over the spot, so that the intestine does not come out: and you have already opened between the patient's legs, and placed a pillow under him, and another servant is on his legs, and another on his chest who holds his hands.
Then place the cautery on this mark, your hand holding the cautery straight.
And hold it until you reach bone with it: or repeat with it a second time, if you did not reach the bone with it on the first try.
And carefully watch for the exit of intestine during your cauterization, lest you burn it, and through that either death or great harm comes upon the patient.
And know that when you do not reach bone with the cautery, your operation is not effective.
And it is necessary that the cautery for children be thin, according to their size.
Then treat with the remaining ointments until it heals.
And let the patient lie on his back for forty days, until the wound seals.
And it is necessary that you arrange his nourishment throughout the duration of his treatment to be that which loosens his belly: so that the intestine does not come out during straining and defecation.
Then when he wants to rise after forty days, then apply a properly made bandage, and let him keep it for another forty days.
And let him reduce labor, and fullness of food and drink, and violent voices.
For when he follows this regimen, he is thus healed with complete healing.
And I will describe the treatment of Ruptures with incision in its chapter.
When however Ruptures occur in the rest of the belly, and they are beginning, and you wish that they not increase, then cauterize its Rupture with a round cautery according to its size: and let that which is burned be like a third of it.
Then treat it with what we have mentioned: and it will not increase.
And some of the ancients have already said: that the Rupture should be cauterized with a triangular cautery, according to this form.
After it is marked with ink, and a line is placed which goes across the upper side of the Rupture, and another line to the lower part.
And place your hand in the middle with a nail-shaped cautery.
But the first cautery is easier and better.
Concerning the method of cauterizing in pains due to falls or blows.
Chapter 48.
When pain occurs in certain limbs from a fall or blow: and that pain persists for a long time, and treatment with medicines is not effective: then it is necessary that it be cauterized with a Point cautery.
And let the cautery of each limb be a cautery according to its size and its smallness, and its weakness and its strength, and the location of the twisting and pain in it.
If therefore it heals from the first cautery, it is well.
If not: then repeat the cautery on it.
For it is the habit of these pains to move from one limb to that which is near it.
Therefore it is necessary that you follow them with the cautery until the patient is healed.
On the Method of Cauterizing in Leprosy.
Chapter 49.
Lepers are sometimes helped by cautery with the greatest benefit.
And especially the type of Leprosy which occurs due to putrefaction of phlegm and melancholy: when therefore you wish to cauterize it, consider the following.
If therefore the Leprosy is beginning, and you have treated it with what we mentioned in the division, and it neither descends nor stays: and you fear for the patient that corruption might overtake his entire constitution: then cauterize him on the head with five cauteries: one in the middle of the known head, and a second lower towards the forehead near the hairline, and two above the corners [of the forehead], and one behind on the nape of the neck.
And [apply] your hand with the cautery gradually, until it makes a small impression in the bone, and scales are displaced from it: so that the expiration of thick vapors from it is relieved, and also cauterize with cautery over the spleen, according to what was previously stated.
But if the Leprosy has already spread over the patient and appears manifestly: then it is necessary that you cauterize with these cauteries which we mentioned in the head, and with cautery on the tip of the nose, and two cauteries on the two jaws, and two cauteries on the vertebrae of the neck, and six on the vertebrae of the back, and one large one on the coccyx near the tail bone and one above it, in the same sacral region: and two on the hips: namely one on each hip, and two on the knees: one on each knee, and two on the shoulders, and two on the elbows, and two on the tender parts of his chest: and cauterize him on every joint of the joints of his hands and feet: and cauterize on every heel of his feet and the bones of his hands.
And beware of the nerves that are on the back of the heel, so that you do not burn them.
And sometimes it is cauterized with cautery over the pubic bone, and another over the stomach bone, and another over the liver.
And know that the more cautery you add, the greater the benefit and the more helpful it is.
And know that the patient does not feel pain from the cautery as healthy people feel it: because his body has already become numb.
And the cauteries should be of size and smallness according to the limbs and joints: according to what was previously stated about the types of iron instruments.
Then treat the cautery with vetch flour with honey, and the remaining treatment, until it heals.
On the Method of Cauterizing in Numbness.
Chapter 50.
When any limb becomes numb, and is treated with medicines, and oils, and plasters, and does not heal, then cauterize the numb limb itself with cauteries, according to what the size of the limb or its smallness deserves.
And let your cautery penetrate slightly into the thickness of the skin.
Then treat it with ointment until it heals.
And sometimes it is cauterized for certain numbness, which occurs in the hand and foot, in the vertebrae of the back near the exit of the nerves, which move that limb: and the numbness is removed.
But let no one presume to do this unless they are knowledgeable in the anatomy of the limbs and the emergence of the nerves moving the body.
On the Method of Cauterizing in Vitiligo.
Chapter 51.
When vitiligo becomes chronic, and nothing from medical treatments helps in it: then cauterize over it with a somewhat deep cautery, according to the thickness of the skin, until the whiteness is removed and its color changes.
Then treat it with vetch flour and lentils with rose oil, and plantain leaves, and dove's blood, and swallow's blood: of each take one part: mix all these, and spread them on a cloth, and apply to the place until it heals.
On the Method of Cauterizing in Cancer.
Chapter 52.
When Cancer is beginning, and you wish to stop it: then cauterize it with a circular cautery around its circumference, as it revolves.
The wise ones however said to cauterize with a final cautery in the middle.
This does not seem right to me: since I fear that it might ulcerate: and I have already seen this several times.
And it is more correct to cauterize around its circumference with a circle, as we said: or with many cauteries.
On the method of cauterizing in Adubelati.
Chapter 53.
When someone has Adubelati, and it is slow to mature, either due to excess matter causing it, or due to the age of the patient, when he is decrepit with little blood, or due to timing, and you wish to hasten the maturation of Adubelati, then cauterize around its circumference with many small cauteries by puncturing.
Then leave it.
For it will hasten with maturation.
If however you wish to perforate it with a cautery, then heat the cautery, which has this form.
And place it in the middle of the Adubelati, until it penetrates the skin: and let the cautery be from that which the patient follows, so that the flow of pus may be relieved.
Then treat it until it heals.
On the method of cauterizing in corrosive disease.
Chapter 54.
Corrosive disease is nothing but corruption moving in a limb, and it corrodes it: like fire consumes dry wood.
If therefore you see corrosive disease in a place that can tolerate cautery with fire, then heat many cauteries, small and large nail-like ones, according to what is suitable for that place where the corrosive disease is.
Then cauterize it from all sides until you eradicate all corruption, and nothing remains of it at all.
Then leave it for three days, and place ground sulfur with oil over the cauterized areas, until all scabs and all corruption are eradicated.
Then treat it with ointments that generate flesh.
If therefore you see that after three days flesh grows with healthy growth, in which there is no corruption, it is good.
And if not: then repeat the cautery over what remains of the corrupted areas.
And corrosive disease is sometimes treated with sharp medicine.
For it rises in place of the cautery.
However, cautery with fire is of swifter benefit: and I indeed have already spoken about its cauterization with sharp medicine in the division: therefore take it there when you need it.
On the method of cauterizing in Nails and Warts.
Chapter 55.
Many times this illness occurs in the lower parts of the feet: and it is a thick, compacted thing, which harms the foot.
And cautery indeed in these is according to two modes: cautery with fire, and cautery with hot water.
As for with fire, it is that you heat a concave cautery similar to a vulture's feather: which should be made of iron, of such size that it contains the nail from all sides: and it should have thin edges.
Then place it heated over the nail.
Then rotate your hand with the cautery around the circumference of the nail, until the cautery reaches the depth of the nail: and leave it for three days, until it begins to emit pus.
Then plaster it with wild mallows, ground with salt: and leave the plaster on it overnight.
For it will be eradicated from its roots.
Then treat the area with flesh-generating ointment until it heals.
But if they are not converted, and frequently occur on the surface of the body, especially on the hands and feet: then administer in them cautery with hot water: that is, take a small tube of brass, or iron, or from a vulture's feather: and place it over the nail, or althelul.
